        </div><div class="casAbstract">The development of new anode materials having high electrochem. performances and interesting reaction mechanisms is highly required to satisfy the need for long-lasting mobile electronic devices and elec. vehicles.  Here, we report a layer cryst. structured SnP3 and its unique electrochem. behaviors with Li.  The SnP3 was simply synthesized through modification of Sn crystallog. by combination with P and its potential as an anode material for LIBs was investigated.  During Li insertion reaction, the SnP3 anode showed an interesting two-step electrochem. reaction mechanism comprised of a topotactic transition (0.7-2.0 V) and a conversion (0.0-2.0 V) reaction.  When the SnP3-based composite electrode was tested within the topotactic reaction region (0.7-2.0 V) between SnP3 and LixSnP3 (x ≤ 4), it showed excellent electrochem. properties, such as a high volumetric capacity (1st discharge/charge capacity was 840/663 mA h cm-3) with a high initial coulombic efficiency, stable cycle behavior (636 mA h cm-3 over 100 cycles), and fast rate capability (550 mA h cm-3 at 3C).  This layered SnP3 anode will be applicable to a new anode material for rechargeable LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoyAzFIMEwhxLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg4dRAdYWJidg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhslGrtL7E&amp;md5=a1a9dc1ed1c0566a7374d42cd712c47c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.7b02039"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, A.-R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, C.-M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Cubic Crystal-Structured SnTe for Superior Li- and Na-Ion Battery Anodes</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>11</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">6074</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">6084</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cubic Crystal-Structured SnTe for Superior Li- and Na-Ion Battery Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Park, Ah-Ram; Park, Cheol-Min</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A cubic crystal-structured Sn-based compd., SnTe, was easily synthesized using a solid-state synthetic process to produce a better rechargeable battery, and its possible application as a Sn-based high-capacity anode material for Li-ion batteries (LIBs) and Na-ion batteries (NIBs) was investigated.  The electrochem. driven phase change mechanisms of the SnTe electrodes during Li and Na insertion/extn. were thoroughly examd. utilizing various ex situ anal. techniques.  During Li insertion, SnTe was converted to Li4.25Sn and Li2Te, meanwhile, during Na insertion, SnTe experienced a sequential topotactic transition to NaxSnTe (x ≤ 1.5) and conversion to Na3.75Sn and Na2Te, which recombined into the original SnTe phase after full Li and Na extn.  The distinctive phase change mechanisms provided remarkable electrochem. Li- and Na-ion storage performances, such as large reversible capacities with high Coulombic efficiencies and stable cyclabilities with fast C-rate characteristics, by prepg. amorphous-C-decorated nanostructured SnTe-based composites.  Therefore, SnTe, with its interesting phase change mechanisms, will be a promising alternative for the oncoming generation of anode materials for LIBs and NIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp71ySACg6_TLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li-O7TVPKsSNg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXntlWis7o%253D&amp;md5=c8c0016d0e95a42d7316c12fed2d0818</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1039/c5ta03181h"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Update on Anode Materials for Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have emerged in recent years, due to their advantages of natural abundance, low cost and environmental friendliness.  In this article, we review the up-to-date research progress on anode materials for Na-ion batteries from five respects: carbon-based materials, alloy-based materials, metal oxides and sulfides based on conversion reaction, titanium-based compds. with insertion mechanism, and org. composites.  In particular, we not only summarize the Na-storage mechanism of these anodes, but also discuss the failure mechanism.  The problems and challenges assocd. with these anodes are pointed out.  Furthermore, on the basis of extensive reports and our exptl. studies, feasible strategies are suggested for designing high performance anode materials.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Silicon Diphosphide: A Si-Based Three-Dimensional Crystalline Framework as a High-Performance Li-Ion Battery Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kwon, Hyuk-Tae; Lee, Churl Kyoung; Jeon, Ki-Joon; Park, Cheol-Min</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The development of an electrode material for rechargeable Li-ion batteries (LIBs) and the understanding of its reaction mechanism play key roles in enhancing the electrochem. characteristics of LIBs for use in various portable electronics and elec. vehicles.  Here, a three-dimensional (3D) cryst.-framework-structured silicon diphosphide (SiP2) and its interesting electrochem. behaviors for superior LIBs are reported.  During Li insertion in the SiP2, a three-step electrochem. reaction mechanism, sequentially comprised of a topotactic transition (0.55-2 V), an amorphization (0.25-2 V), and a conversion (0-2 V), was thoroughly analyzed.  On the basis of the three-step electrochem. reaction mechanism, excellent electrochem. properties, such as high initial capacities, high initial Coulombic efficiencies, stable cycle behaviors, and fast-rate capabilities, were attained from the prepn. of a nanostructured SiP2/C composite.  This 3D cryst.-framework-structured SiP2 compd. will be a promising alternative anode material in the realization and mass prodn. of excellent, rechargeable LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpJuAjrEHCocrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lif4l54DUk8AQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XptVSisrw%253D&amp;md5=97069fd8935608a63a6907519246fe10</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201209689"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High Capacity and Rate Capability of Amorphous Phosphorus for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Angew.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Phosphorus-carbon nanocomposite anodes for lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ramireddy, Thrinathreddy; Xing, Tan; Rahman, Md Mokhlesur; Chen, Ying; Dutercq, Quentin; Gunzelmann, Daniel; Glushenkov, Alexey M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5572-5584</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">With the expected theor. capacity of 2596 mA h g-1, P is considered to be the highest capacity anode material for Na-ion batteries and one of the most attractive anode materials for Li-ion systems.  This work presents a comprehensive study of P-C nanocomposite anodes for both Li-ion and Na-ion batteries.  The composite electrodes are able to display high initial capacities of ∼1700 and 1300 mA h g-1 in Li and Na half-cells, resp., when the cells are tested within a larger potential windows of 2.0-0.01 V vs. Li/Li+ and Na/Na+.  The level of demonstrated capacity is underpinned by the storage mechanism, based on the transformation of P to Li3P phase for Li cells and an incomplete transformation to Na3P phase for Na cells.  The capacity deteriorates upon cycling, which is shown to originate from disintegration of electrodes and their delamination from current collectors by post-cycling ex situ electron microscopy.  Stable cyclic performance at the level of ∼700 and ∼350-400 mA h g-1 can be achieved if the potential windows are restricted to 2.0-0.67 V vs. Li/Li+ for Li and 2-0.33 vs. Na/Na+ for Na half-cells.  The results are critically discussed in light of literature reports.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpbpTdmNtgwtrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgUISh4vCeh_Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXit1aqt7o%253D&amp;md5=964498820e44c8f37b2e4e369def7076</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1038/nnano.2015.194"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, H.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pasta, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Phosphorene–Graphene Hybrid Material as a High-Capacity Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Nat.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A phosphorene-graphene hybrid material as a high-capacity anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Jie; Lee, Hyun-Wook; Pasta, Mauro; Yuan, Hongtao; Zheng, Guangyuan; Sun, Yongming; Li, Yuzhang; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Nanotechnology</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">980-985</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have recently attracted significant attention as an alternative to Li-ion batteries because Na sources do not present the geopolitical issues that Li sources might.  Although recent reports on cathode materials for Na-ion batteries demonstrated performances comparable to their Li-ion counterparts, the major scientific challenge for a competitive Na-ion battery technol. is to develop viable anode materials.  A hybrid material made out of a few phosphorene layers sandwiched between graphene layers shows a specific capacity of 2 440 mA h g-1 (calcd. using the mass of P only) at a c.d. of 0.05 A g-1 and an 83% capacity retention after 100 cycles while operating between 0 and 1.5 V.  Using in situ TEM and ex situ x-ray diffraction techniques, the authors explain the large capacity of the anode through a dual mechanism of intercalation of Na ions along the x axis of the phosphorene layers followed by the formation of a Na3P alloy.  The presence of graphene layers in the hybrid material works as a mech. backbone and an elec. highway, ensuring that a suitable elastic buffer space accommodates the anisotropic expansion of phosphorene layers along the y and z axial directions for stable cycling operation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp8p8kp9p5tl7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgUISh4vCeh_Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsV2ltrrM&amp;md5=23b94375b97b50394801c280ff017cb8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2018.07.026"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nam, K.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jeon, K.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, C.-M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Layered Germanium Phosphide-Based Anodes for High-Performance Lithium- and Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>17</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">78</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">87</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A controlled red phosphorus@Ni-P core@shell nanostructure as an ultralong cycle-life and superior high-rate anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Shuai; Feng, Jinkui; Bian, Xiufang; Liu, Jie; Xu, Hui; An, Yongling</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1222-1233</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), a potential alternative to lithium ion batteries (LIBs), have attracted remarkable attention recently due to the natural abundance and low-cost of sodium.  Here, we have presented a comprehensive study on combining electroless deposition with chem. dealloying to control the shell thickness and compn. of a red phosphorus (RP)@Ni-P core@shell nanostructure as a high performance anode for SIBs.  For the first time depending on regulating the dealloying time (1 h, 4 h, 8 h, 10 h and 20 h) of RP@Ni-P synthesized by electroless deposition of Ni on RP, 1 h RP@Ni-P, 4 h RP@Ni-P, 8 h RP@Ni-P, 10 h RP@Ni-P and 20 h RP@Ni-P with different shell thicknesses and compns. were prepd.  The in situ generated Ni2P on RP particle surfaces can facilitate intimate contact between RP and a mech. strong amorphous Ni-P outer shell with a high electronic cond., which ensures strong electrode structural integrity, a stable solid electrolyte interphase and ultra-fast electronic transport.  As a result, the 8 h RP@Ni-P composite presents a super high capacity (1256.2 mA h gcomposite-1 after 200 cycles at 260 mA gcomposite-1), superior rate capability (491 mA h gcomposite-1 at 5200 mA gcomposite-1) and unprecedented ultralong cycle-life at 5000 mA gcomposite-1 for an RP-based SIB anode (409.1 mA h gcomposite-1 after 2000 cycles).  This simple scalable synthesis approach will provide a new strategy for the optimization of core@shell nanostructures, paving the way for mass prodn. of high performance electrodes for SIBs and other energy storage systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoVRwOrxeWHubVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgUISh4vCeh_Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXlsVyqurg%253D&amp;md5=5a9d70a9ec338f9b2bf0d110723db337</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1039/c6ta00103c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Duveau, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Israel, S.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pioneer study of SiP2 as negative electrode for Li- and Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Duveau, D.; Israel, S.         </div><div class="casAbstract">For the first time it is demonstrated that a dense SiP2 pyrite-type obtained by a very simple ball milling method delivers outstanding capacity in both lithium and sodium batteries with up to 1000 mA h g-1 and 572 mA h g-1 sustained after 30 and 15 cycles resp.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrw3A20fZ42TbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgUISh4vCeh_Q"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical GeP5/Carbon Nanocomposite with Dual-Carbon Conductive Network as Promising Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ning, Qiu-Li; Hou, Bao-Hua; Wang, Ying-Ying; Liu, Dao-Sheng; Luo, Zhong-Zhen; Li, Wen-Hao; Yang, Yang; Guo, Jin-Zhi; Wu, Xing-Long</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to the Earth's scarcity of Li, replacing Li with earth-abundant and low-cost Na for Na-ion batteries (SIBs) has recently become a promising substitute for Li-ion batteries.  However, the shortage of appropriate anode materials limits the development of SIBs.  Here, a dual-C conductive network enhanced GeP5 (GeP5/acetylene black/partially reduced graphene oxide sheets (GeP5/AB/p-rGO)) composite is prepd. by a facile ball milling method.  The dual-C network not only provides more transport pathways for electrons but also relaxes the huge vol. change of the electrode material during the charge/discharge process.  Compared with only AB- or GO-modified GeP5 (GeP5/AB or GeP5/GO) composite, the GeP5/AB/p-rGO composite shows a superior Na storage performance with an excellent rate and cycle performance.  It delivers a high reversible capacity of 597.5 and 175 mAh/g at the c.d. of 0.1 and 5.0 A/g, resp.  At the c.d. of 0.5 A/g, the GeP5/AB/p-rGO composite shows the reversible capacity of 400 mAh/g after 50 cycles with a little capacity attenuation.  All above results prove that the GeP5/AB/p-rGO composite has a good prospect of application as an anode material for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo60mEYO-Dlf7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhma731Z7Mtxw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhvVehs7nO&amp;md5=cda6c0bb19d5802251c8ce0980fcca83</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2018.01.358"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">GeP<sub>5</sub>/C Composite as Anode Material for High Power Sodium-Ion Batteries with Exceptional Capacity</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">GeP5/C composite as anode material for high power sodium-ion batteries with exceptional capacity</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yujie; Xiao, Xuezhang; Fan, Xiulin; Li, Meng; Zhang, Yiwen; Zhang, Wei; Chen, Lixin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">744</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">15-22</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Red phosphorus (P) as anode materials for sodium ion battery has an obvious superiority in high theor. capacity (2600 mAh/g), but its elec. cond. is not ideal.  Alloying red P and other elementary substance is an effective method to improve this situation.  Here in, we synthesize a type of GeP5/C composite by high energy ball milling method, and use this composite as anode for sodium-ion battery.  The structure morphol. and electrochem. performance of the GeP5/C composite have been investigated in detail.  The GeP5/C composite delivers a high first discharge capacity of 1368 mAh/g and a satisfactory initial coulumbic efficiency of 88.3% at a c.d. of 150 mA/g.  Even at an ultrahigh c.d. of 5000 mA/g, it still delivers a higher discharge capacity of 839.6 mAh/g and better capacity retention of 59.2% over 30 cycles, compared with those of pure GeP5.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synergistic Na-Storage Reactions in Sn4P3 as a High-Capacity, Cycle-stable Anode of Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qian, Jiangfeng; Xiong, Ya; Cao, Yuliang; Ai, Xinping; Yang, Hanxi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1865-1869</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Room-temp. Na-ion batteries have attracted great interest as a low cost and environmentally benign technol. for large scale elec. energy storage, however their development is hindered by the lack of suitable anodic host materials.  In this paper, a green approach is described for the synthesis of Sn4P3/C nanocomposite and demonstrated its excellent Na-storage performance as a novel anode of Na-ion batteries.  This Sn4P3/C anode can deliver a very high reversible capacity of 850 mA h g-1 with a remarkable rate capability with 50% capacity output at 500 mA g-1 and can also be cycled with 86% capacity retention over 150 cycles due to a synergistic Na-storage mechanism in the Sn4P3 anode, where the Sn nanoparticles act as electronic channels to enable electrochem. activation of the P component, while the elemental P and its sodiated product Na3P serve as a host matrix to alleviate the aggregation of the Sn particles during Na insertion reaction.  This mechanism may offer a new approach to create high capacity and cycle-stable alloy anodes for Na-ion batteries and other electrochem. energy storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrQCCVmbohfnbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhma731Z7Mtxw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXjvFSiurg%253D&amp;md5=1c703e0dccdc2b5cea071abf02396265</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201500174"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Suo, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liou, S.-C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Superior Stable Self-Healing SnP<sub>3</sub> Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Charge-Discharge Properties of a Sn4P3 Negative Electrode in Ionic Liquid Electrolyte for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Usui, Hiroyuki; Domi, Yasuhiro; Fujiwara, Kohei; Shimizu, Masahiro; Yamamoto, Takayuki; Nohira, Toshiyuki; Hagiwara, Rika; Sakaguchi, Hiroki</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1139-1143</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We evaluated the charge-discharge performance of a Sn4P3 neg. electrode in an ionic liq. electrolyte comprised of N-methyl-N-propylpyrrolidinium bis(fluorosulfonyl)amide (Py13-FSA) and NaFSA.  We also conducted cyclic voltammetry and transmission electron microscopy for the Sn4P3 electrode to reveal the reaction mechanism.  It was suggested that Na15Sn4 and Na3P are formed via phase sepn. in the first sodiation and that elemental Sn and elemental P formed by following a desodiation reaction with Na ions in the subsequent cycles.  The Sn4P3 electrode exhibited a high Coulombic efficiency of 99.1% at the fourth cycle and an excellent cycling performance with a high reversible capacity of 750 mA h g-1 even at the 200th cycle.  We demonstrated that there are two important factors to improve the performance: (i) higher vol. fraction of Sn than P and (ii) uniform dispersion of Sn nanoparticles in a P matrix.  The ionic liq. electrolyte showed good applicability to the Sn4P3 neg. electrode due to its superior electrochem. stability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrsO05rReIo8LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh461m8sqLsRw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXmsVaiu74%253D&amp;md5=f6c746861d2cac107354f1e7223ed166</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201600376"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ge, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Low-Temperature Solution-Based Phosphorization Reaction Route to Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>/Reduced Graphene Oxide Nanohybrids as Anodes for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries (SIB) have potential for large scale renewable energy storage due to geopolitical abundance of Na.  However, the high capacity Na-ion anodes still suffer from poor cycling stability and low Coulombic efficiency (CE).  Herein, uniform Sn4P3@C spheres were synthesized by a facile aerosol spray-pyrolysis-phosphidation method.  By tuning the electrolyte, a reversible capacity of ∼ 800 mAh/g with an extremely low capacity decay rate of 0.09% per cycle was achieved with a record-high initial CE (&gt; 90%) and high cyclic CE (∼ 99.9%).  The Sn4P3@C in the stable ether-based electrolyte shows the highest accumulated cycling capacities in the reported SIB anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp7KyxRXvJpSLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh461m8sqLsRw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhtVWqsbrJ&amp;md5=26b3d738a89939782d7ba9d3c9289210</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1039/c8ta01492b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kravchyk, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ibáñez, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Krumeich, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Widmer, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nasiou, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Meyns, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Llorca, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Arbiol, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kovalenko, M.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">SnP nanocrystals as anode materials for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Junfeng; Wang, Shutao; Kravchyk, Kostiantyn; Ibanez, Maria; Krumeich, Frank; Widmer, Roland; Nasiou, Despina; Meyns, Michaela; Llorca, Jordi; Arbiol, Jordi; Kovalenko, Maksym V.; Cabot, Andreu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">23</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10958-10966</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Tin monophosphide is a layered material consisting of Sn-P-P-Sn sandwiches that are stacked on top of each other to form a three dimensional crystallog. structure.  Its compn. and crystal structure makes it an excellent candidate anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, SnP is yet to be explored for such and other applications due to its challenging synthesis.  In the present work, we report the synthesis of SnP nanocrystals (NCs) from the reaction of hexamethylphosphorous triamide (HMPT) and a tin phosphonate prepd. from tin oxalate and a long chain phosphonic acid.  SnP NCs obtained from this reaction displayed a spherical geometry and a trigonal crystallog. phase with a superstructure attributed to ordered diphosphorus pairs.  Such NCs were mixed with carbon black and used as anode materials in SIBs.  SIBs based on SnP NCs and sodium(I) bis(fluorosulfonyl)imide (NaFSI) electrolyte displayed a high reversible capacity of 600 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 and cycling stability for over 200 cycles.  Their excellent cycling performance is assocd. with both the small size of the crystal domains and the particular compn. and phase of SnP which prevent mech. disintegration and major phase sepn. during sodiation and desodiation cycles.  These results demonstrate SnP to be an attractive anode material for sodium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrjCRGLHJcTg7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liZExFWIhc4hA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXpsVWqsrg%253D&amp;md5=efc97b6bdde872f5980a56f32e047b5a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1039/c4cc09604e"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chou, S.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.-Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.-K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S.-X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A New, Cheap, and Productive FeP Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rational Design of Three-Dimensional Graphene Encapsulated with Hollow FeP@Carbon Nanocomposite as Outstanding Anode Material for Lithium Ion and Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Xiujuan; Chen, Kai; Wang, Gang; Liu, Xiaojie; Wang, Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11602-11616</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal phosphides have been extensively investigated owing to their high theor. capacities and relatively low intercalation potentials vs Li/Li+, but their practical applications have been hindered by low elec. cond. and dramatic vol. variation during cycling.  In this work, an interesting strategy for the rational design of graphene (GR) encapsulated with a hollow FeP@carbon nanocomposite (H-FeP@C@GR) via a combination of a hydrothermal route, a carbon-coating process, phosphidation treatment, and carbothermic reaction is reported.  The hollow FeP (H-FeP) nanospheres shelled with thin carbon layers are wonderfully incorporated into the GR matrix, interconnecting to form a three-dimensional (3D) hierarchical architecture.  Such a design offers distinct advantages for FeP-based anode materials for both lithium ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  For example, the 3D omnibearing conductive networks from the GR skeleton and outer coating carbon can provide an open freeway for electron/ion transport, promoting the electrode reaction kinetics.  In addn., the wrapping of an H-FeP nanosphere in a thin carbon layer enables the formation of a solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) on the carbon layer surface instead of on the individual H-FeP surface, preventing the continual re-forming of the SEI.  When used as anode materials for LIBs and SIBs, H-FeP@C@GR exhibited excellent electrochem. performances.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoJNbfRlD70dbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liZExFWIhc4hA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhs1yhsbnP&amp;md5=60e49fafbda32645938e58b743ba2e5d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2018.03.009"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lim, Y.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon-coated CoP3 nanocomposites as anode materials for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Wenxi; Ma, Xiaoqing; Wang, Guangzhao; Long, Xiaojiang; Li, Yadong; Zhang, Wanli; Zhang, Peng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Applied Surface Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">445</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">It still remains a great challenge to develop a high-performance anode for sodium ion batteries.  In this work, carbon-coated CoP3(CoP3@C) nanocomposites have been obtained by a high energy mech. milling and used as an anode of sodium ion battery for the first time, showing a larger discharge capacity, longer cycling life and better rate capability as compared to plain CoP3.  The superior performance is not only originated from significantly enhanced diffusion kinetics assocg. with the improvement of electron cond. and vol. change based on the presence of carbon layer, but also attributed to the partially pseudocapacitive behaviors of the redox reaction to construct a rapid electron transport pathway.  In addn., the XRD and TEM anal. reveal that the Na-storage mechanism of the CoP3@C anode involves a conversion reaction from CoP3 to Na3P and metallic Co at the initial discharge and charge state.  This study also provides a significant strategy to design special hybrid materials with excellent sodium storage capability for meeting the demand of large-scale energy storage systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr7w-Ge-VVntbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liZExFWIhc4hA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXmt1aiu7s%253D&amp;md5=65fc01ee9a60fef614ea0f0ef61fd51d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2016.11.055"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ge, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Metal-Organic Frameworks Derived Porous Core/Shell CoP@C Polyhedrons Anchored on 3D Reduced Graphene Oxide Networks as Anode for Sodium-Ion Battery</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>32</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">117</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">124</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Metal-organic frameworks derived porous core/shellCoP@C polyhedrons anchored on 3D reduced graphene oxide networks as anode for sodium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ge, Xiaoli; Li, Zhaoqiang; Yin, Longwei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">32</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel strategy is developed to synthesize metal-org. framework (MOF) derived core/shell structured CoP@C polyhedrons anchored on 3D reduced grapheme oxide (RGO) on nickel foam (NF) as binder-free anode for high performance sodium-ion battery, through an in-situ low-temp. phosphidation process from ZIF-67 derived core/shell Co@C polyhedral structures.  The unique CoP@C-RGO-NF binder-free anode exhibits a remarkable electrochem. performance with outstanding cycling stability and high rate capability, delivering a specific capacity of 473.1 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 100 cycles.  The excellent properties can be attributed to synergistic effects between core/shell CoP@C polyhedrons and RGO networks.  The unique core/shell CoP@C polyhedrons can offer more electrode/electrolyte contact area and reduce the diffusion distance of Na+, while carbon layer shell can enhance electronic cond. and buffer vol. change, and prevent CoP from pulverization and aggregation.  Furthermore, 3D RGO networks can provide adequate surface areas for a high loading content of CoP and enhance charge transfer kinetics.  Meanwhile, RGO/NF can efficiently act as a binder and elec. conductor to interconnect the sep. CoP@C polyhedrons.  The present strategy for CoP@C-RGO-NF architectures can be extended to other novel electrodes for high performance energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoEA0RBe_Ev_LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhRut-rXhM5pw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitFGiurfO&amp;md5=95bf6b3529a8069bf6929d1f00eeaf34</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b00444"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Metal–Organic Frameworks-Derived Co<sub>2</sub>P@N-C@RGO with Dual Protection Layers for Improved Sodium Storage</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanostructured CuP2/C composites as high-performance anode materials for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Feipeng; Han, Na; Huang, Wenjing; Li, Jiaojiao; Ye, Hualin; Chen, Fengjiao; Li, Yanguang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

                        cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cross-Linking Hollow Carbon Sheet Encapsulated CuP2 Nanocomposites for High Energy Density Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Shuangqiang; Wu, Feixiang; Shen, Laifa; Huang, Yuanye; Sinha, Shyam Kanta; Srot, Vesna; van Aken, Peter A.; Maier, Joachim; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7018-7027</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries (SIB) are regarded as the most promising competitors to Li-ion batteries in spite of expected electrochem. disadvantages.  Here a crosslinking strategy is proposed to mitigate the typical SIB problems.  We present a SIB full battery that exhibits a working potential of 3.3 V and an energy d. of 180 Wh/Kg with good cycle life.  The anode is composed of crosslinking hollow C sheet-encapsulated CuP2 nanoparticles (CHCS-CuP2) and a cathode of C-coated Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (C-NVPF).  For the prepn. of the CHCS-CuP2 nanocomposites, we develop an in situ phosphorization approach, which is superior to mech. mixing.  Such CHCS-CuP2 nanocomposites deliver a high reversible capacity of 451 mAh/g at 80 mA/g, showing an excellent capacity retention ratio of 91% in 200 cycles together with good rate capability and stable cycling performance.  Post mortem anal. reveals that the crosslinking hollow carbon sheet structure as well as the initially formed SEI layers are well preserved.  The inner electrochem. resistances do not significantly change.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Molybdenum Phosphide: A Conversion-type Anode for Ultralong-Life Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Zhaodong; Hou, Hongshuai; Wang, Chao; Li, Simin; Zhang, Yun; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High specific capacity and long cycling life of anode materials still remain major challenges in the development of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Nowadays, transition metal phosphides have been reckoned as promising anodes in view of their high theor. specific capacities, low potential for sodium storage, and superior cond.  Herein, molybdenum phosphide (MoP) nanorods wrapped with thin carbon layer have been prepd. and applied as an anode for SIBs.  By utilizing in situ X-ray diffraction technol., a conversion-type mechanism of MoP anode has been disclosed.  This kind of MoP electrode exhibits extraordinary electrochem. properties, including excellent cycling performance with a discharge capacity of 398.4 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 800 cycles, and remarkable rate capabilities, which remain 104.5 mA g-1 at 1600 mA h g-1 even after 10,000 loops.  The distinguished performances stem from synergetic merits of the morphol., structure, and mechanism of MoP.  It is expected that MoP will be a promising anode material for SIBs and this work would provide theor. basis for the scalable research and applications of MoP-based anode materials for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoc3DRJ12UzbLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lioRF-1zrIZng"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhtlWnsr3N&amp;md5=42db05d069cc8ce6437cbfdfc241593d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2017.07.016"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Self-Supported Zn<sub>3</sub>P<sub>2</sub> Nanowires-Assembly Bundles Grafted on Ti Foil as an Advanced Integrated Electrodes for Lithium/Sodium Ion Batteries with High Performances</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-supported Zn3P2 nanowires-assembly bundles grafted on Ti foil as an advanced integrated electrodes for lithium/sodium ion batteries with high performances</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Xinwei; Li, Wenwu; Yu, Jiale; Zhang, Haiyan; Shi, Zhicong; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">724</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Well-aligned Zn3P2 nanowires-assembly bundles/Ti foil integrated anodes were for the first time successfully synthesized by a facile chem. vapor deposition.  When directly applied as anodes for lithium/sodium ion batteries, they show excellent lithium/sodium storage performance esp. in high-rate capability.  Specifically, applied as anode material for lithium ion batteries, it showed 1100 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles and an ultrahigh rate performance with 300 mA h g-1 even at 40 A g-1; as anode material for sodium ion batteries, it was, for the first time, investigated and delivered a high initial specific capacity of 1120 mA h g-1, and excellent rate capability with 280 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1, demonstrating that Zn3P2 nanowires-assembly bundles/Ti foil integrated anodes are a promising anode candidate for lithium/sodium ion batteries.  The Ex-situ x-ray diffraction and HRTEM were for the first time, carried out to investigate the sodium storage mechanism of Zn3P2.  Such superior lithium/sodium storage performances can be attributed to this well-aligned Zn3P2 nanowires-assembly bundles structure, which not only mitigates the vol. expansion of Zn3P2 during cycling but also provides the direct electron transfer to ensure high-rate performances.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrtWzypTylGhLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lioRF-1zrIZng"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXht1entrjM&amp;md5=b880c44cc19d2ec6bb53bf8d9e364934</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">De Podesta, M.</span></span> <i>Understanding the Properties of Matter</i>, <span class="NLM_edition">2</span>nd ed.; <span class="NLM_publisher-name">Taylor &amp; Francis</span>: <span class="NLM_publisher-loc">London</span>, <span class="NLM_year">2001</span>.</span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26publication_year%3D2001%26author%3DM.%2BDe%2BPodesta%26title%3DUnderstanding%2Bthe%2BProperties%2Bof%2BMatter&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b21803&amp;doiOfLink=&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The mechanism of the electrochem. reaction of Zn with Li was studied by ex situ XRD anal. combined with a differential capacity plot of the Zn electrode at a low current of 10 mA/g.  The pure Zn electrode showed a high reactivity with Li, with 1st discharge and charge capacities of 574 and 351 mA-h/g, resp. Based on these analyses, an interesting partial recombination reaction of ZnO is discovered, which demonstrates that Li2O formed during Li insertion is partially reversible.  Addnl., we discover that the control of the partial recombination reaction of the metal oxide is very important for improving reversibility in the first cycle, which is a key finding for realization of highly reversible oxide-based electrode materials. The as-synthesized cubes were found to be derived from the self-assembly of ZnSnO3 nanoparticles.  A hollow interior was subsequently obtained through a facile etching reaction.  A reversible capacity of 315 mA h g-1 (∼0.3 V vs. Na+/Na) was obtained when cycled between 0.01 and 3.00 V vs. Na+/Na at 30 mA g-1.  A decent capacity retention of 92% was also obsd. after 100 cycles when tested at 250 mA g-1.  The ZnSnO3 hollow cubes were found to demonstrate superior electrochem. performance when compared with both ZnSnO3 solid cubes and manually blended ZnO-SnO2.  The enhanced performance is believed to be attributed to the even distribution of Zn and Sn metallic nanoparticles following the first conversion process, which, conversely, is unachievable in manually blended ZnO-SnO2.  Addnl. free space owing to different vol. expansions during alloying of Zn and Sn easily permits diffusion of Na+ to the interior of the microcube, giving rise to enhanced capacity and cyclability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqBqsJcmxe_lLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0linbLumcp9RfQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rationally designed carbon coated ZnSnS3 nano cubes as high-performance anode for advanced sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jia, Hao; Dirican, Mahmut; Chen, Chen; Zhu, Pei; Yan, Chaoyi; Li, Ya; Zhu, Jiadeng; Li, Zhaoling; Guo, Jiansheng; Zhang, Xiangwu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">292</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">646-654</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal sulfides have gradually gained attention as preferable anode materials in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to their high theor. capacities.  In this work, we report for the first time the synthesis of carbon coated ZnSnS3 nanocubes (ZnSnS3@C NCs) as high-performance anode material for SIBs.  The outer carbon coating surrounding the ZnSnS3 active material not only enhances the electronic cond. of the anode but also increases the electrode reaction active sites.  Thus, it can greatly improve the reversible capacity as well as homogenize the repeated vol. changes of the active material and decrease the mech. stress caused during the prolonged charge/discharge process, which could finally enable an enhanced electrode stability.  Electrochem. test results demonstrated that the introduced ZnSnS3@C NC anode is capable of delivering a high reversible capacity of 661.4 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 250 cycles (with capacity retention of 97.1%) and demonstrating a stable Coulombic efficiency of over 99%.  To the best of our knowledge, both the reversible capacity and cycling stability performance introduced in this work are so far the best among metallic sulfur-based anodes and are even superior to some recently reported SnS2-based anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoSjmOSv7doXLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh0Zb41zZ-udA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit63R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">63</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Overpotential-Dependent Phase Transformation Pathways in Lithium Iron Phosphate Battery Electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kao, Yu-Hua; Tang, Ming; Meethong, Nonglak; Bai, Jianming; Carter, W. Craig; Chiang, Yet-Ming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2010</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">An objective in battery development for higher storage energy d. is the design of compds. that can accommodate max. changes in ion concn. over useful electrochem. windows.  Not surprisingly, many storage compds. undergo phase transitions in situ, including prodn. of metastable phases.  Unique to this environment is the frequent application of elec. overpotentials and underpotentials, which are the elec. analogs to undercooling and superheating.  Surprisingly, overpotential effects on phase stability and transformation mechanisms have not been studied in detail.  Here we use synchrotron x-ray diffraction performed in situ during potentiostatic and galvanostatic cycling, combined with phase-field modeling, to reveal a remarkable dependence of phase transition pathway on overpotential in the model olivine Li1-xFePO4.  For a sample of particle size ∼113 nm, at both low (e.g., &lt;20 mV) and high (&gt;75 mV) overpotentials a crystal-to-crystal olivine transformation dominates, whereas at intermediate overpotentials a cryst.-to-amorphous phase transition is preferred.  As particle sizes decrease to the nanoscale, amorphization is further emphasized.  Implications for battery use and design are considered.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp89bDYv4cumrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljUYAX31sD4Jw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3cXht12jtb3P&amp;md5=142c2fdbbf7b7604bef0eef5e8ab3aca</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref64"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref64'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">64</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit64" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2019.02.046"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ovejas, V.                         cas_cit64R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">64</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">State of charge dependency of the overvoltage generated in commercial Li-ion cells</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ovejas, V. J.; Cuadras, A.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The overvoltage that is produced in the cells under operation limits the capacity and power they can deliver.  A detailed study about the mechanisms that contribute to that overvoltage, and thus to their lifetime, is required for optimizing the use of batteries as well as their manufg. process.  The authors study galvanostatic discharge at low and moderate rates in an LCO-NMC/graphite cell to quantify the ohmic voltage drop and activation and concn. polarizations.  For doing so, the authors compare half-cells to full cell overvoltages.  The ohmic drop and concn. polarization dominate at high rates and low rates, resp.  Also, the authors track the evolution of concn. polarization with State-of-Charge (SoC) and there exists a relation between diffusion and phase transformations.  Specifically, the authors validate exptl. that initial stages of a phase formation are not dominated by diffusion.  Phase transitions are commonly evaluated by incremental capacity anal.  However, it is more appropriate to obtain that information from the full cells by the overvoltage anal.  Also, probably the working SoC range can should be optimized from the overvoltage anal. by avoiding the particular SoCs at which the most detrimental phase transitions take place.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq-nHcOVAQGr7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljUYAX31sD4Jw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXjsVensbk%253D&amp;md5=40d090990496781891b4ac6af5fd891f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref65"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref65'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">65</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit65" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.8b00586"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, M.-G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, D.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jung, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, J.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, C.-M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sn-Based Nanocomposite for Li-Ion Battery Anode with High Energy Density, Rate Capability, and Reversibility</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2955</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2967</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsnano.8b00586</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D12%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D2955-2967%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DM.-G.%2BPark%26author%3DD.-H.%2BLee%26author%3DH.%2BJung%26author%3DJ.-H.%2BChoi%26author%3DC.-M.%2BPark%26title%3DSn-Based%2BNanocomposite%2Bfor%2BLi-Ion%2BBattery%2BAnode%2Bwith%2BHigh%2BEnergy%2BDensity%252C%2BRate%2BCapability%252C%2Band%2BReversibility%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsnano.8b00586&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b21803&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsnano.8b00586&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit65R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">65</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sn-Based Nanocomposite for Li-Ion Battery Anode with High Energy Density, Rate Capability, and Reversibility</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Park, Min-Gu; Lee, Dong-Hun; Jung, Heechul; Choi, Jeong-Hee; Park, Cheol-Min</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2955-2967</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">To design an easily manufd., large energy d., highly reversible, and fast rate-capable Li-ion battery (LIB) anode, Co-Sn intermetallics (CoSn2, CoSn, and Co3Sn2) were synthesized, and their potential as anode materials for LIBs was investigated.  Based on their electrochem. performances, CoSn2 was selected, and its C-modified nanocomposite (CoSn2/C) as well as Ti- and C-modified nanocomposite (CoSn2/a-TiC/C) was straightforwardly prepd.  Interestingly, the CoSn2, CoSn2/C, and CoSn2/a-TiC/C showed conversion/nonrecombination, conversion/partial recombination, and conversion/full recombination during Li insertion/extn., resp., which were thoroughly investigated using ex situ x-ray diffraction and extended x-ray absorption fine structure analyses.  As a result of the interesting conversion/full recombination mechanism, the easily manufd. CoSn2/a-TiC/C nanocomposite for the Sn-based Li-ion battery anode showed large energy d. (first reversible capacity of 1399 mAh cm-3), high reversibility (first Coulombic efficiency of 83.2%), long cycling behavior (100% capacity retention after 180 cycles), and fast rate capability (approx. 1110 mAh cm-3 at 3C rate).  In addn., degrdn./enhancement mechanisms for high-capacity and high-performance Li-alloy-based anode materials for next-generation LIBs were also suggested.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqsVnHV0JUi_bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhlRl1VHxrnnA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXjvFGgtbo%253D&amp;md5=ce6f220f577855b7388a6985adef80b5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref66"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref66'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">66</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit66" data-doi="10.1149/2.1161709jes"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nam, K.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, J.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, C.-M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Highly Reversible Na-Ion Reaction in Nanostructured Sb<sub>2</sub>Te<sub>3</sub>-C Composites as Na-Ion Battery Anodes</span>. <i>J. Electrochem. Soc.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>164</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">A2056</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">A2064</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1149/2.1161709jes</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D164%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3DA2056-A2064%26journal%3DJ.%2BElectrochem.%2BSoc.%26author%3DK.-H.%2BNam%26author%3DJ.-H.%2BChoi%26author%3DC.-M.%2BPark%26title%3DHighly%2BReversible%2BNa-Ion%2BReaction%2Bin%2BNanostructured%2BSb2Te3-C%2BComposites%2Bas%2BNa-Ion%2BBattery%2BAnodes%26doi%3D10.1149%252F2.1161709jes&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b21803&amp;doiOfLink=10.1149%2F2.1161709jes&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit66R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">66</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly Reversible Na-Ion Reaction in Nanostructured Sb2Te3-C Composites as Na-Ion Battery Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nam, Ki-Hun; Choi, Jeong-Hee; Park, Cheol-Min</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">164</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">A2056-A2064</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JESOAN</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4651</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Electrochemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sb2Te3 and its amorphous C-modified nanocomposite (Sb2Te3-C) are synthesized by simple solid-state synthetic methods, and their potential as anode materials for rechargeable Na-ion batteries (NIBs) is evaluated.  Ex situ x-ray diffraction and high-resoln. TEM clearly demonstrate the sodiation/desodiation reaction mechanism of the Sb2Te3 and Sb2Te3-C nanocomposite electrodes.  In both electrodes, Sb2Te3 is converted into Na3Sb and Na2Te during Na insertion.  However, Na3Sb and Na2Te in only the Sb2Te3-C nanocomposite electrode recombine into the original Sb2Te3 phase after full Na extn.  As a consequence of its interesting conversion/recombination reaction during sodiation/desodiation reaction, the Sb2Te3-C nanocomposite electrode exhibits a long cycle life with highly reversible gravimetric and volumetric capacity (373 mA h g-1 and 765 mA h cm-3 over 50 cycles) and fast rate capability (1 C: 391 mA h g-1 and 802 mA h cm-3; 2 C: 377 mA h g-1 and 773 mA h cm-3).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrLHgpoxQFT6LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhlRl1VHxrnnA"> &gt;&gt;
