<span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tong, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Review of Carbon Materials and Their Composites with Alloy Metals for Sodium Ion Battery Anodes</span>. <i>Carbon</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>98</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">162</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">178</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.carbon.2015.09.091</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D98%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D162-178%26journal%3DCarbon%26author%3DM.-S.%2BBalogun%26author%3DY.%2BLuo%26author%3DW.%2BQiu%26author%3DP.%2BLiu%26author%3DY.%2BTong%26title%3DA%2BReview%2Bof%2BCarbon%2BMaterials%2Band%2BTheir%2BComposites%2Bwith%2BAlloy%2BMetals%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBattery%2BAnodes%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.carbon.2015.09.091&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b21803&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.carbon.2015.09.091&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit67R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">67</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A review of carbon materials and their composites with alloy metals for sodium ion battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Balogun, Muhammad-Sadeeq; Luo, Yang; Qiu, Weitao; Liu, Peng; Tong, Yexiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">98</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">162-178</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CRBNAH</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0008-6223</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries are currently emerging as a replacement for lithium ion batteries due to sodium abundance in the earth's crust.  The recent development of sodium ion batteries anode has been achieved by the use of selected carbon as an anode.  The performance of the selected carbon materials such as the charge/discharge capacity, voltage profile and cyclic stability, depend strongly on the sizes, additives, electrolytes and structures.  Based on the contribution of the carbon-based materials as a replacement of the sodium ion batteries anode, much improvement has been achieved.  However, more investigations are still required in order to identify the suitable carbon materials that can provide and improve the anode properties.  In the same vein, alloy materials have gained increasing effort as high capacity anode and their combination with carbon have contributed to the development of sodium ion batteries.  In this review, we have accounted for the development of carbon-based materials and their composites with alloy materials as well as their prospects and challenges for sodium ion battery anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqLqTy97T_9sLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhlRl1VHxrnnA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvVOmsbvM&amp;md5=5bc4c118e6be905d663496bf2953e8d7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref68"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref68'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">68</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit68" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2019.05.047"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nam, K.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, C.-M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">2D Layered Sb<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>-Based Amorphous Composite for High-Performance Li- and Na-Ion Battery Anodes</span>. <i>J. Power Sources</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>433</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">126639</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">126647</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2019.05.047</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D433%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D126639-126647%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DK.-H.%2BNam%26author%3DC.-M.%2BPark%26title%3D2D%2BLayered%2BSb2Se3-Based%2BAmorphous%2BComposite%2Bfor%2BHigh-Performance%2BLi-%2Band%2BNa-Ion%2BBattery%2BAnodes%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2019.05.047&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b21803&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2019.05.047&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit68R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">68</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">2D layered Sb2Se3-based amorphous composite for high-performance Li- and Na-ion battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nam, Ki-Hun; Park, Cheol-Min</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">433</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">126639</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A two-dimensional layered Sb2Se3-based amorphous composite (a-Sb2Se3/C) is synthesized using a simple solid-state ball-milling process, and its potential for Li- and Na-ion batteries is evaluated.  Ex situ extended X-ray absorption fine structure analyses clearly indicate the electrochem. reaction mechanisms of Sb2Se3 and a-Sb2Se3/C as anodes for Li- and Na-ion batteries.  During Li- and Na-insertion, the Sb2Se3 and a-Sb2Se3/C electrodes are converted into the final phases of Li3Sb/Na3Sb and Li2Se/Na2Se, resp.  During Li- and Na-extn., the Li3Sb/Na3Sb and Li2Se/Na2Se in the Sb2Se3 electrode are converted into Sb and Se, showing a non-recovery reaction, whereas a recovery to the original Sb2Se3 in the a-Sb2Se3/C electrode occurs after full Li and Na extn.  Owing to the interesting conversion/recovery reaction, the a-Sb2Se3/C electrode exhibits excellent electrochem. performance, such as high reversible capacities (Li-ion battery: 662 mAh g-1; Na-ion battery: 407 mAh g-1), a long cycle life with highly reversible capacities (Li-ion battery: 662 mAh g-1 and 1,205 mAh cm-3, resp., after 100th cycle; Na-ion battery: 378 mAh g-1 and 688 mAh cm-3, resp., after 50th cycle), and high rate capabilities (Li-ion battery: 623 mAh g-1 and 1,133 mAh cm-3 at 3C; Na-ion battery: 270 mAh g-1 and 492 mAh cm-3 at 2C).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a                 clearInterval(recommendCheckInterval);
                googletag.cmd.push(function() { googletag.display("dfp-journal-article-recommend"); });
            }
        }, 100);
    });
    </script>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Energy prodn. and storage have become key issues concerning our welfare in daily life.  Present challenges for batteries are twofold.  In the first place, the increasing demand for powering systems of portable electronic devices and zero-emission vehicles stimulates research towards high energy and high voltage systems.  In the second place, low cost batteries are required in order to advance towards smart elec. grids that integrate discontinuous energy flow from renewable sources, optimizing the performance of clean energy sources.  Na-ion batteries can be the key for the second point, because of the huge availability of sodium, its low price and the similarity of both Li and Na insertion chemistries.  In spite of the lower energy d. and voltage of Na-ion based technologies, they can be focused on applications where the wt. and footprint requirement is less drastic, such as elec. grid storage.  Much work has to be done in the field of Na-ion in order to catch up with Li-ion technol.  Cathodic and anodic materials must be optimized, and new electrolytes will be the key point for Na-ion success.  This review will gather the up-to-date knowledge about Na-ion battery materials, with the aim of providing a wide view of the systems that have already been explored and a starting point for the new research on this battery technol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRYtxfVVW_sLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li9sb13yU_s8w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XivFWnu7s%253D&amp;md5=72869139086b8ee9adec746418ff84b1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1021/cr500192f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yabuuchi, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kubota, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dahbi, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komaba, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Re-search Development on Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, lithium-ion batteries were attracting more interest for use in automotive applications.  Lithium resources are confirmed to be unevenly distributed in South America, and the cost of the lithium raw materials has roughly doubled from the first practical application in 1991 to the present and is increasing due to global demand for lithium-ion accumulators.  Since the electrochem. equiv. and std. potential of sodium are the most advantageous after lithium, sodium based energy storage is of great interest to realize lithium-free high energy and high voltage batteries.  However, to the best of authors knowledge, there were no successful reports on electrochem. sodium insertion materials for battery applications; the major challenge is the neg. electrode and its passivation.  In this study, high capacity and excellent reversibility are achieved of sodium-insertion performance of hard-carbon and layered NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 electrodes in propylene carbonate electrolyte solns.  The structural change and passivation for hard-carbon are investigated to study the reversible sodium insertion.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The intermittent nature of renewable energy sources, such as solar and wind, calls for sustainable elec. energy storage (EES) technologies for stationary applications.  Li will be simply too rare for Li-ion batteries (LIBs) to be used for large-scale storage purposes.  In contrast, Na-ion batteries (NIBs) are highly promising to meet the demand of grid-level storage because Na is truly earth abundant and ubiquitous around the globe.  Furthermore, NIBs share a similar rocking-chair operation mechanism with LIBs, which potentially provides high reversibility and long cycling life.  It would be most efficient to transfer knowledge learned on LIBs during the last three decades to the development of NIBs.  Following this logic, rapid progress has been made in NIB cathode materials, where layered metal oxides and polyanionic compds. exhibit encouraging results.  On the anode side, pure graphite as the std. anode for LIBs can only form NaC64 in NIBs if solvent co-intercalation does not occur due to the unfavorable thermodn.  In fact, it was the utilization of a carbon anode in LIBs that enabled the com. successes.  Anodes of metal-ion batteries det. key characteristics, such as safety and cycling life; thus, it is indispensable to identify suitable anode materials for NIBs.In this Account, we review recent development on anode materials for NIBs.  Due to the limited space, we will mainly discuss carbon-based and alloy-based anodes and highlight progress made in our groups in this field.  We first present what is known about the failure mechanism of graphite anode in NIBs.  We then go on to discuss studies on hard carbon anodes, alloy-type anodes, and org. anodes.  Esp., the multiple functions of natural cellulose that is used as a low-cost carbon precursor for mass prodn. and as a soft substrate for tin anodes are highlighted.  The strategies of minimizing the surface area of carbon anodes for improving the first-cycle Coulombic efficiency are also outlined, where graphene oxide was employed as dehydration agent and 2,2,6,6-tetramethylpiperidine-1-oxyl (TEMPO) was used to unzip wood fiber.  Furthermore, surface modification by at. layer deposition technol. is introduced, where we discover that a thin layer of Al2O3 can function to encapsulate Sn nanoparticles, leading to a much enhanced cycling performance.  We also highlight recent work about the phosphorene/graphene anode, which outperformed other anodes in terms of capacity.  The arom. org. anode is also studied as anode with very high initial sodiation capacity.  Furthermore, electrochem. intercalation of Na ions into reduced graphene oxide is applied for fabricating transparent conductors, demonstrating the great feasibility of Na ion intercalation for optical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGorKnQvVSK3P7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgeryt9I5QvYg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtVGksrg%253D&amp;md5=90d2907a2b33fdcf59913255073dd969</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref8" class="rightTabRefNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit8" data-doi="10.1149/1.3607983"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chevrier, V. The authors examine the viability of Na-ion anode materials based on Na alloys or hard carbons in terms of volumetric energy d.  Due to the bigger size of the Na atom compared to the Li atom, Na alloys would lead to anode materials with about half the volumetric energy d. of their Li analogs. The SnP3 was simply synthesized through modification of Sn crystallog. by combination with P and its potential as an anode material for LIBs was investigated.  During Li insertion reaction, the SnP3 anode showed an interesting two-step electrochem. reaction mechanism comprised of a topotactic transition (0.7-2.0 V) and a conversion (0.0-2.0 V) reaction.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A cubic crystal-structured Sn-based compd., SnTe, was easily synthesized using a solid-state synthetic process to produce a better rechargeable battery, and its possible application as a Sn-based high-capacity anode material for Li-ion batteries (LIBs) and Na-ion batteries (NIBs) was investigated.  The electrochem. driven phase change mechanisms of the SnTe electrodes during Li and Na insertion/extn. were thoroughly examd. utilizing various ex situ anal. techniques.  During Li insertion, SnTe was converted to Li4.25Sn and Li2Te, meanwhile, during Na insertion, SnTe experienced a sequential topotactic transition to NaxSnTe (x ≤ 1.5) and conversion to Na3.75Sn and Na2Te, which recombined into the original SnTe phase after full Li and Na extn.  The distinctive phase change mechanisms provided remarkable electrochem. Li- and Na-ion storage performances, such as large reversible capacities with high Coulombic efficiencies and stable cyclabilities with fast C-rate characteristics, by prepg. amorphous-C-decorated nanostructured SnTe-based composites.  Therefore, SnTe, with its interesting phase change mechanisms, will be a promising alternative for the oncoming generation of anode materials for LIBs and NIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp71ySACg6_TLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgeryt9I5QvYg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXntlWis7o%253D&amp;md5=c8c0016d0e95a42d7316c12fed2d0818</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref11" class="rightTabRefNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit11" data-doi="10.1039/c5ta03181h"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Update on Anode Materials for Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">With the expected theor. capacity of 2596 mA h g-1, P is considered to be the highest capacity anode material for Na-ion batteries and one of the most attractive anode materials for Li-ion systems.  This work presents a comprehensive study of P-C nanocomposite anodes for both Li-ion and Na-ion batteries.  The composite electrodes are able to display high initial capacities of ∼1700 and 1300 mA h g-1 in Li and Na half-cells, resp., when the cells are tested within a larger potential windows of 2.0-0.01 V vs. Li/Li+ and Na/Na+.  The level of demonstrated capacity is underpinned by the storage mechanism, based on the transformation of P to Li3P phase for Li cells and an incomplete transformation to Na3P phase for Na cells.  The capacity deteriorates upon cycling, which is shown to originate from disintegration of electrodes and their delamination from current collectors by post-cycling ex situ electron microscopy.  Stable cyclic performance at the level of ∼700 and ∼350-400 mA h g-1 can be achieved if the potential windows are restricted to 2.0-0.67 V vs. Li/Li+ for Li and 2-0.33 vs. Na/Na+ for Na half-cells.  The results are critically discussed in light of literature reports.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpbpTdmNtgwtrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0litYeZ6rOYmtw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXit1aqt7o%253D&amp;md5=964498820e44c8f37b2e4e369def7076</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref18" class="rightTabRefNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit18" data-doi="10.1038/nnano.2015.194"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, H.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pasta, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Phosphorene–Graphene Hybrid Material as a High-Capacity Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Nat.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have recently attracted significant attention as an alternative to Li-ion batteries because Na sources do not present the geopolitical issues that Li sources might.  Although recent reports on cathode materials for Na-ion batteries demonstrated performances comparable to their Li-ion counterparts, the major scientific challenge for a competitive Na-ion battery technol. is to develop viable anode materials.  A hybrid material made out of a few phosphorene layers sandwiched between graphene layers shows a specific capacity of 2 440 mA h g-1 (calcd. using the mass of P only) at a c.d. of 0.05 A g-1 and an 83% capacity retention after 100 cycles while operating between 0 and 1.5 V. The presence of graphene layers in the hybrid material works as a mech. backbone and an elec. highway, ensuring that a suitable elastic buffer space accommodates the anisotropic expansion of phosphorene layers along the y and z axial directions for stable cycling operation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp8p8kp9p5tl7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0litYeZ6rOYmtw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsV2ltrrM&amp;md5=23b94375b97b50394801c280ff017cb8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref19" class="rightTabRefNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit19" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2018.07.026"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nam, K.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jeon, K.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, C.-M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Layered Germanium Phosphide-Based Anodes for High-Performance Lithium- and Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>17</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">78</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">87</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), a potential alternative to lithium ion batteries (LIBs), have attracted remarkable attention recently due to the natural abundance and low-cost of sodium.  Here, we have presented a comprehensive study on combining electroless deposition with chem. dealloying to control the shell thickness and compn. of a red phosphorus (RP)@Ni-P core@shell nanostructure as a high performance anode for SIBs.  For the first time depending on regulating the dealloying time (1 h, 4 h, 8 h, 10 h and 20 h) of RP@Ni-P synthesized by electroless deposition of Ni on RP, 1 h RP@Ni-P, 4 h RP@Ni-P, 8 h RP@Ni-P, 10 h RP@Ni-P and 20 h RP@Ni-P with different shell thicknesses and compns. were prepd.  The in situ generated Ni2P on RP particle surfaces can facilitate intimate contact between RP and a mech. strong amorphous Ni-P outer shell with a high electronic cond., which ensures strong electrode structural integrity, a stable solid electrolyte interphase and ultra-fast electronic transport.  As a result, the 8 h RP@Ni-P composite presents a super high capacity (1256.2 mA h gcomposite-1 after 200 cycles at 260 mA gcomposite-1), superior rate capability (491 mA h gcomposite-1 at 5200 mA gcomposite-1) and unprecedented ultralong cycle-life at 5000 mA gcomposite-1 for an RP-based SIB anode (409.1 mA h gcomposite-1 after 2000 cycles).  This simple scalable synthesis approach will provide a new strategy for the optimization of core@shell nanostructures, paving the way for mass prodn. of high performance electrodes for SIBs and other energy storage systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoVRwOrxeWHubVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0litYeZ6rOYmtw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXlsVyqurg%253D&amp;md5=5a9d70a9ec338f9b2bf0d110723db337</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref21" class="rightTabRefNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit21" data-doi="10.1039/c6ta00103c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Duveau, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Israel, S.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to the Earth's scarcity of Li, replacing Li with earth-abundant and low-cost Na for Na-ion batteries (SIBs) has recently become a promising substitute for Li-ion batteries.  However, the shortage of appropriate anode materials limits the development of SIBs.  Here, a dual-C conductive network enhanced GeP5 (GeP5/acetylene black/partially reduced graphene oxide sheets (GeP5/AB/p-rGO)) composite is prepd. by a facile ball milling method.  The dual-C network not only provides more transport pathways for electrons but also relaxes the huge vol. change of the electrode material during the charge/discharge process.  Compared with only AB- or GO-modified GeP5 (GeP5/AB or GeP5/GO) composite, the GeP5/AB/p-rGO composite shows a superior Na storage performance with an excellent rate and cycle performance.  It delivers a high reversible capacity of 597.5 and 175 mAh/g at the c.d. of 0.1 and 5.0 A/g, resp.  At the c.d. of 0.5 A/g, the GeP5/AB/p-rGO composite shows the reversible capacity of 400 mAh/g after 50 cycles with a little capacity attenuation.  All above results prove that the GeP5/AB/p-rGO composite has a good prospect of application as an anode material for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo60mEYO-Dlf7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgUZ9JXkfK5fA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhvVehs7nO&amp;md5=cda6c0bb19d5802251c8ce0980fcca83</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref23" class="rightTabRefNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit23" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2018.01.358"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">GeP<sub>5</sub>/C Composite as Anode Material for High Power Sodium-Ion Batteries with Exceptional Capacity</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Red phosphorus (P) as anode materials for sodium ion battery has an obvious superiority in high theor. capacity (2600 mAh/g), but its elec. cond. is not ideal.  Alloying red P and other elementary substance is an effective method to improve this situation.  Here in, we synthesize a type of GeP5/C composite by high energy ball milling method, and use this composite as anode for sodium-ion battery.  The structure morphol. and electrochem. performance of the GeP5/C composite have been investigated in detail.  The GeP5/C composite delivers a high first discharge capacity of 1368 mAh/g and a satisfactory initial coulumbic efficiency of 88.3% at a c.d. of 150 mA/g.  Even at an ultrahigh c.d. of 5000 mA/g, it still delivers a higher discharge capacity of 839.6 mAh/g and better capacity retention of 59.2% over 30 cycles, compared with those of pure GeP5.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Room-temp. Na-ion batteries have attracted great interest as a low cost and environmentally benign technol. for large scale elec. energy storage, however their development is hindered by the lack of suitable anodic host materials.  In this paper, a green approach is described for the synthesis of Sn4P3/C nanocomposite and demonstrated its excellent Na-storage performance as a novel anode of Na-ion batteries.  This Sn4P3/C anode can deliver a very high reversible capacity of 850 mA h g-1 with a remarkable rate capability with 50% capacity output at 500 mA g-1 and can also be cycled with 86% capacity retention over 150 cycles due to a synergistic Na-storage mechanism in the Sn4P3 anode, where the Sn nanoparticles act as electronic channels to enable electrochem. activation of the P component, while the elemental P and its sodiated product Na3P serve as a host matrix to alleviate the aggregation of the Sn particles during Na insertion reaction.                         rightTab-cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Charge-Discharge Properties of a Sn4P3 Negative Electrode in Ionic Liquid Electrolyte for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Usui, Hiroyuki; Domi, Yasuhiro; Fujiwara, Kohei; Shimizu, Masahiro; Yamamoto, Takayuki; Nohira, Toshiyuki; Hagiwara, Rika; Sakaguchi, Hiroki</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">We evaluated the charge-discharge performance of a Sn4P3 neg. electrode in an ionic liq. electrolyte comprised of N-methyl-N-propylpyrrolidinium bis(fluorosulfonyl)amide (Py13-FSA) and NaFSA.  We also conducted cyclic voltammetry and transmission electron microscopy for the Sn4P3 electrode to reveal the reaction mechanism.  It was suggested that Na15Sn4 and Na3P are formed via phase sepn. in the first sodiation and that elemental Sn and elemental P formed by following a desodiation reaction with Na ions in the subsequent cycles.  The Sn4P3 electrode exhibited a high Coulombic efficiency of 99.1% at the fourth cycle and an excellent cycling performance with a high reversible capacity of 750 mA h g-1 even at the 200th cycle.  We demonstrated that there are two important factors to improve the performance: (i) higher vol. fraction of Sn than P and (ii) uniform dispersion of Sn nanoparticles in a P matrix.  The ionic liq. electrolyte showed good applicability to the Sn4P3 neg. electrode due to its superior electrochem. stability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrsO05rReIo8LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgUZ9JXkfK5fA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXmsVaiu74%253D&amp;md5=f6c746861d2cac107354f1e7223ed166</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref27" class="rightTabRefNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit27" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201600376"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ge, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Low-Temperature Solution-Based Phosphorization Reaction Route to Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>/Reduced Graphene Oxide Nanohybrids as Anodes for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Tin monophosphide is a layered material consisting of Sn-P-P-Sn sandwiches that are stacked on top of each other to form a three dimensional crystallog. structure.  Its compn. and crystal structure makes it an excellent candidate anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, SnP is yet to be explored for such and other applications due to its challenging synthesis.  In the present work, we report the synthesis of SnP nanocrystals (NCs) from the reaction of hexamethylphosphorous triamide (HMPT) and a tin phosphonate prepd. from tin oxalate and a long chain phosphonic acid.  SnP NCs obtained from this reaction displayed a spherical geometry and a trigonal crystallog. phase with a superstructure attributed to ordered diphosphorus pairs.  Such NCs were mixed with carbon black and used as anode materials in SIBs.  SIBs based on SnP NCs and sodium(I) bis(fluorosulfonyl)imide (NaFSI) electrolyte displayed a high reversible capacity of 600 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 and cycling stability for over 200 cycles.  Their excellent cycling performance is assocd. with both the small size of the crystal domains and the particular compn. and phase of SnP which prevent mech. disintegration and major phase sepn. during sodiation and desodiation cycles.  These results demonstrate SnP to be an attractive anode material for sodium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrjCRGLHJcTg7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li750PAVbRPTA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXpsVWqsrg%253D&amp;md5=efc97b6bdde872f5980a56f32e047b5a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref31" class="rightTabRefNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit31" data-doi="10.1039/c4cc09604e"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chou, S.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.-Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.-K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S.-X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A New, Cheap, and Productive FeP Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal phosphides have been extensively investigated owing to their high theor. capacities and relatively low intercalation potentials vs Li/Li+, but their practical applications have been hindered by low elec. cond. and dramatic vol. variation during cycling.  In this work, an interesting strategy for the rational design of graphene (GR) encapsulated with a hollow FeP@carbon nanocomposite (H-FeP@C@GR) via a combination of a hydrothermal route, a carbon-coating process, phosphidation treatment, and carbothermic reaction is reported.  The hollow FeP (H-FeP) nanospheres shelled with thin carbon layers are wonderfully incorporated into the GR matrix, interconnecting to form a three-dimensional (3D) hierarchical architecture.  Such a design offers distinct advantages for FeP-based anode materials for both lithium ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  For example, the 3D omnibearing conductive networks from the GR skeleton and outer coating carbon can provide an open freeway for electron/ion transport, promoting the electrode reaction kinetics.  In addn., the wrapping of an H-FeP nanosphere in a thin carbon layer enables the formation of a solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) on the carbon layer surface instead of on the individual H-FeP surface, preventing the continual re-forming of the SEI.                         rightTab-cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon-coated CoP3 nanocomposites as anode materials for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Wenxi; Ma, Xiaoqing; Wang, Guangzhao; Long, Xiaojiang; Li, Yadong; Zhang, Wanli; Zhang, Peng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Applied Surface Science</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">It still remains a great challenge to develop a high-performance anode for sodium ion batteries.  In this work, carbon-coated CoP3(CoP3@C) nanocomposites have been obtained by a high energy mech. milling and used as an anode of sodium ion battery for the first time, showing a larger discharge capacity, longer cycling life and better rate capability as compared to plain CoP3.  The superior performance is not only originated from significantly enhanced diffusion kinetics assocg. with the improvement of electron cond. and vol. change based on the presence of carbon layer, but also attributed to the partially pseudocapacitive behaviors of the redox reaction to construct a rapid electron transport pathway.  In addn., the XRD and TEM anal. reveal that the Na-storage mechanism of the CoP3@C anode involves a conversion reaction from CoP3 to Na3P and metallic Co at the initial discharge and charge state.  This study also provides a significant strategy to design special hybrid materials with excellent sodium storage capability for meeting the demand of large-scale energy storage systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr7w-Ge-VVntbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li750PAVbRPTA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXmt1aiu7s%253D&amp;md5=65fc01ee9a60fef614ea0f0ef61fd51d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref35" class="rightTabRefNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit35" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2016.11.055"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ge, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Metal-Organic Frameworks Derived Porous Core/Shell CoP@C Polyhedrons Anchored on 3D Reduced Graphene Oxide Networks as Anode for Sodium-Ion Battery</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>32</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">117</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">124</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        rightTab-cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Metal-organic frameworks derived porous core/shellCoP@C polyhedrons anchored on 3D reduced graphene oxide networks as anode for sodium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ge, Xiaoli; Li, Zhaoqiang; Yin, Longwei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel strategy is developed to synthesize metal-org. framework (MOF) derived core/shell structured CoP@C polyhedrons anchored on 3D reduced grapheme oxide (RGO) on nickel foam (NF) as binder-free anode for high performance sodium-ion battery, through an in-situ low-temp. phosphidation process from ZIF-67 derived core/shell Co@C polyhedral structures.  The unique CoP@C-RGO-NF binder-free anode exhibits a remarkable electrochem. performance with outstanding cycling stability and high rate capability, delivering a specific capacity of 473.1 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 100 cycles.  The excellent properties can be attributed to synergistic effects between core/shell CoP@C polyhedrons and RGO networks.  The unique core/shell CoP@C polyhedrons can offer more electrode/electrolyte contact area and reduce the diffusion distance of Na+, while carbon layer shell can enhance electronic cond. and buffer vol. change, and prevent CoP from pulverization and aggregation.  Furthermore, 3D RGO networks can provide adequate surface areas for a high loading content of CoP and enhance charge transfer kinetics.  Meanwhile, RGO/NF can efficiently act as a binder and elec. conductor to interconnect the sep. CoP@C polyhedrons.  The present strategy for CoP@C-RGO-NF architectures can be extended to other novel electrodes for high performance energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoEA0RBe_Ev_LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li750PAVbRPTA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitFGiurfO&amp;md5=95bf6b3529a8069bf6929d1f00eeaf34</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref36" class="rightTabRefNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit36" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b00444"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Metal–Organic Frameworks-Derived Co<sub>2</sub>P@N-C@RGO with Dual Protection Layers for Improved Sodium Storage</span>. <i>ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Research on Na ion batteries has recently been revived.  Attention is now placed on the development of high-capacity and stable electrode materials at low costs.  Among them, compds. operating on the conversion mechanism represent a promising class of anode materials.  Unfortunately, they are generally plagued by poor elec. cond. and large vol. changes during repeated cycling.  The authors exploit a new type of composite material made of Cu phosphide and Super P C black (CuP2/C) as a potential anode candidate.  The final products consisted of cryst. CuP2 cores coated with C black nanoparticles on the surface.  Electrochem. measurements and multiple ex situ studies demonstrate that CuP2/C composites are capable of fast and reversible sodiation and desodiation based on the conversion mechanism.  They deliver a large capacity &gt;500 mA-h g-1, high rate capability and decent short-term cycling stability.  Probably these transition metal phosphides with a suitable C coating may hold great opportunities as anode materials for Na ion batteries for effective and economical energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpNvcGwcWr-prVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg_9y1F7wD07Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsV2ltL%252FO&amp;md5=5e274a266f214959ed90f3db240495e8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref39" class="rightTabRefNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit39" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.8b02721"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sinha, S.                         rightTab-cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cross-Linking Hollow Carbon Sheet Encapsulated CuP2 Nanocomposites for High Energy Density Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Shuangqiang; Wu, Feixiang; Shen, Laifa; Huang, Yuanye; Sinha, Shyam Kanta; Srot, Vesna; van Aken, Peter A.; Maier, Joachim; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries (SIB) are regarded as the most promising competitors to Li-ion batteries in spite of expected electrochem. disadvantages.  Here a crosslinking strategy is proposed to mitigate the typical SIB problems.  We present a SIB full battery that exhibits a working potential of 3.3 V and an energy d. of 180 Wh/Kg with good cycle life.  The anode is composed of crosslinking hollow C sheet-encapsulated CuP2 nanoparticles (CHCS-CuP2) and a cathode of C-coated Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (C-NVPF).  For the prepn. of the CHCS-CuP2 nanocomposites, we develop an in situ phosphorization approach, which is superior to mech. mixing.  Such CHCS-CuP2 nanocomposites deliver a high reversible capacity of 451 mAh/g at 80 mA/g, showing an excellent capacity retention ratio of 91% in 200 cycles together with good rate capability and stable cycling performance.  Post mortem anal. reveals that the crosslinking hollow carbon sheet structure as well as the initially formed SEI layers are well preserved.  The inner electrochem. resistances do not significantly change.  We believe that this battery system provides significant progress regarding practical application of SIB.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoGGkzfTynAyrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg_9y1F7wD07Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXht1Oqu7vJ&amp;md5=534bba20d2bf1766dfef7be1a4c552a2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref40" class="rightTabRefNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit40" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201604015"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kopold, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">van Aken, P.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The progress on sodium-ion battery technol. faces many grand challenges, one of which is the considerably lower rate of sodium insertion/deinsertion in electrode materials due to the larger size of sodium (Na) ions and complicated redox reactions compared to the lithium-ion systems.  Here, it is demonstrated that sodium ions can be reversibly stored in Zn-Sb intermetallic nanowires at speeds that can exceed 295 nm s-1.  Remarkably, these values are one to three orders of magnitude higher than the sodiation rate of other nanowires electrochem. tested with in situ transmission electron micro-scopy.  It is found that the nanowires display about 161% vol. expansion after the first sodiation and then cycle with an 83% reversible vol. expansion.  Despite their massive expansion, the nanowires can be cycled without any cracking or facture during the ultrafast sodiation/desodiation process.  In addn., most of the phases involved in the sodiation/desodiation process possess high elec. cond.  More specifically, the NaZnSb exhibits a layered structure, which provides channels for fast Na+ diffusion.         </div><div class="casAbstract">An objective in battery development for higher storage energy d. is the design of compds. that can accommodate max. changes in ion concn. over useful electrochem. windows.  Not surprisingly, many storage compds. undergo phase transitions in situ, including prodn. of metastable phases.  Unique to this environment is the frequent application of elec. overpotentials and underpotentials, which are the elec. analogs to undercooling and superheating.  Surprisingly, overpotential effects on phase stability and transformation mechanisms have not been studied in detail.  Here we use synchrotron x-ray diffraction performed in situ during potentiostatic and galvanostatic cycling, combined with phase-field modeling, to reveal a remarkable dependence of phase transition pathway on overpotential in the model olivine Li1-xFePO4.  For a sample of particle size ∼113 nm, at both low (e.g., &lt;20 mV) and high (&gt;75 mV) overpotentials a crystal-to-crystal olivine transformation dominates, whereas at intermediate overpotentials a cryst.-to-amorphous phase transition is preferred.  As particle sizes decrease to the nanoscale, amorphization is further emphasized.  Implications for battery use and design are considered.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp89bDYv4cumrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liicroV56rDhg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3cXht12jtb3P&amp;md5=142c2fdbbf7b7604bef0eef5e8ab3aca</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref64"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref64" class="rightTabRefNumLink">64</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit64" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2019.02.046"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ovejas, V. The authors study galvanostatic discharge at low and moderate rates in an LCO-NMC/graphite cell to quantify the ohmic voltage drop and activation and concn. polarizations.  For doing so, the authors compare half-cells to full cell overvoltages.  The ohmic drop and concn. polarization dominate at high rates and low rates, resp.  Also, the authors track the evolution of concn. polarization with State-of-Charge (SoC) and there exists a relation between diffusion and phase transformations.  Specifically, the authors validate exptl. that initial stages of a phase formation are not dominated by diffusion.  Phase transitions are commonly evaluated by incremental capacity anal.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">To design an easily manufd., large energy d., highly reversible, and fast rate-capable Li-ion battery (LIB) anode, Co-Sn intermetallics (CoSn2, CoSn, and Co3Sn2) were synthesized, and their potential as anode materials for LIBs was investigated.  Based on their electrochem. performances, CoSn2 was selected, and its C-modified nanocomposite (CoSn2/C) as well as Ti- and C-modified nanocomposite (CoSn2/a-TiC/C) was straightforwardly prepd.  Interestingly, the CoSn2, CoSn2/C, and CoSn2/a-TiC/C showed conversion/nonrecombination, conversion/partial recombination, and conversion/full recombination during Li insertion/extn., resp., which were thoroughly investigated using ex situ x-ray diffraction and extended x-ray absorption fine structure analyses.  As a result of the interesting conversion/full recombination mechanism, the easily manufd. CoSn2/a-TiC/C nanocomposite for the Sn-based Li-ion battery anode showed large energy d. (first reversible capacity of 1399 mAh cm-3), high reversibility (first Coulombic efficiency of 83.2%), long cycling behavior (100% capacity retention after 180 cycles), and fast rate capability (approx. 1110 mAh cm-3 at 3C rate).  In addn., degrdn./enhancement mechanisms for high-capacity and high-performance Li-alloy-based anode materials for next-generation LIBs were also suggested.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqsVnHV0JUi_bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liicroV56rDhg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXjvFGgtbo%253D&amp;md5=ce6f220f577855b7388a6985adef80b5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref66"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref66" class="rightTabRefNumLink">66</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit66" data-doi="10.1149/2.1161709jes"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nam, K.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, J.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, C.-M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Highly Reversible Na-Ion Reaction in Nanostructured Sb<sub>2</sub>Te<sub>3</sub>-C Composites as Na-Ion Battery Anodes</span>. <i>J. Electrochem. Soc.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>164</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">A2056</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">A2064</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1149/2.1161709jes</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit66R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">66</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly Reversible Na-Ion Reaction in Nanostructured Sb2Te3-C Composites as Na-Ion Battery Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nam, Ki-Hun; Choi, Jeong-Hee; Park, Cheol-Min</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">164</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">A2056-A2064</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JESOAN</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4651</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Electrochemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sb2Te3 and its amorphous C-modified nanocomposite (Sb2Te3-C) are synthesized by simple solid-state synthetic methods, and their potential as anode materials for rechargeable Na-ion batteries (NIBs) is evaluated.  Ex situ x-ray diffraction and high-resoln. TEM clearly demonstrate the sodiation/desodiation reaction mechanism of the Sb2Te3 and Sb2Te3-C nanocomposite electrodes.  In both electrodes, Sb2Te3 is converted into Na3Sb and Na2Te during Na insertion.  However, Na3Sb and Na2Te in only the Sb2Te3-C nanocomposite electrode recombine into the original Sb2Te3 phase after full Na extn.  As a consequence of its interesting conversion/recombination reaction during sodiation/desodiation reaction, the Sb2Te3-C nanocomposite electrode exhibits a long cycle life with highly reversible gravimetric and volumetric capacity (373 mA h g-1 and 765 mA h cm-3 over 50 cycles) and fast rate capability (1 C: 391 mA h g-1 and 802 mA h cm-3; 2 C: 377 mA h g-1 and 773 mA h cm-3).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrLHgpoxQFT6LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liicroV56rDhg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhtlWnsLvP&amp;md5=8af1f194a8a5043446e7d16ece525d23</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref67"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref67" class="rightTabRefNumLink">67</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit67" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2015.09.091"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Balogun, M.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tong, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Review of Carbon Materials and Their Composites with Alloy Metals for Sodium Ion Battery Anodes</span>. <i>Carbon</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>98</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">162</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">178</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.carbon.2015.09.091</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit67R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">67</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A review of carbon materials and their composites with alloy metals for sodium ion battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Balogun, Muhammad-Sadeeq; Luo, Yang; Qiu, Weitao; Liu, Peng; Tong, Yexiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">98</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">162-178</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CRBNAH</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0008-6223</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries are currently emerging as a replacement for lithium ion batteries due to sodium abundance in the earth's crust.  The recent development of sodium ion batteries anode has been achieved by the use of selected carbon as an anode.  The performance of the selected carbon materials such as the charge/discharge capacity, voltage profile and cyclic stability, depend strongly on the sizes, additives, electrolytes and structures.  Based on the contribution of the carbon-based materials as a replacement of the sodium ion batteries anode, much improvement has been achieved.  However, more investigations are still required in order to identify the suitable carbon materials that can provide and improve the anode properties.  In the same vein, alloy materials have gained increasing effort as high capacity anode and their combination with carbon have contributed to the development of sodium ion batteries.  In this review, we have accounted for the development of carbon-based materials and their composites with alloy materials as well as their prospects and challenges for sodium ion battery anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqLqTy97T_9sLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liicroV56rDhg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvVOmsbvM&amp;md5=5bc4c118e6be905d663496bf2953e8d7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref68"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref68" class="rightTabRefNumLink">68</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit68" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2019.05.047"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nam, K.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, C.-M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">2D Layered Sb<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>-Based Amorphous Composite for High-Performance Li- and Na-Ion Battery Anodes</span>. <i>J. Power Sources</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>433</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">126639</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">126647</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2019.05.047</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit68R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">68</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">2D layered Sb2Se3-based amorphous composite for high-performance Li- and Na-ion battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nam, Ki-Hun; Park, Cheol-Min</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">433</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">126639</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A two-dimensional layered Sb2Se3-based amorphous composite (a-Sb2Se3/C) is synthesized using a simple solid-state ball-milling process, and its potential for Li- and Na-ion batteries is evaluated.  Ex situ extended X-ray absorption fine structure analyses clearly indicate the electrochem. reaction mechanisms of Sb2Se3 and a-Sb2Se3/C as anodes for Li- and Na-ion batteries.  During Li- and Na-insertion, the Sb2Se3 and a-Sb2Se3/C electrodes are converted into the final phases of Li3Sb/Na3Sb and Li2Se/Na2Se, resp.  During Li- and Na-extn., the Li3Sb/Na3Sb and Li2Se/Na2Se in the Sb2Se3 electrode are converted into Sb and Se, showing a non-recovery reaction, whereas a recovery to the original Sb2Se3 in the a-Sb2Se3/C electrode occurs after full Li and Na extn.  Owing to the interesting conversion/recovery reaction, the a-Sb2Se3/C electrode exhibits excellent electrochem. performance, such as high reversible capacities (Li-ion battery: 662 mAh g-1; Na-ion battery: 407 mAh g-1), a long cycle life with highly reversible capacities (Li-ion battery: 662 mAh g-1 and 1,205 mAh cm-3, resp., after 100th cycle; Na-ion battery: 378 mAh g-1 and 688 mAh cm-3, resp., after 50th cycle), and high rate capabilities (Li-ion battery: 623 mAh g-1 and 1,133 mAh cm-3 at 3C; Na-ion battery: 270 mAh g-1 and 492 mAh cm-3 at 2C).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqHvNdFu3_QHrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liicroV56rDhg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhtV2jsrzO&amp;md5=b4e5c49be26a94495dd80c47b1495c04</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i13">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acsami.9b21803?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acsami.9b21803</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Additional Zn–P binary phase diagram; XRD patterns of synthesized ZnP<sub>2</sub>; Zn K-edge EXAFS spectra of Zn, ZnP<sub>2</sub>, and Zn<sub>3</sub>P<sub>2</sub>; XRD pattern and discharge–charge curves of black P; electrochemical behavior of ZnP<sub>2</sub> electrode; SEM image with a PSA result for ZnP<sub>2</sub>-C; EIS analysis results for ZnP<sub>2</sub> and ZnP<sub>2</sub>-C; electrochemical performance of BM-C; SEM images and PSA results for bulk Zn and Zn-C; ex situ XRD results for bulk Zn; Zn K-edge EXAFS spectra of Zn-C at the fully sodiated state; Zn K-edge EXAFS fitting parameters for ZnP<sub>2</sub> and Zn<sub>3</sub>P<sub>2</sub>; Zn-C at the fully sodiated state; and comparison of electrochemical performance of metal phosphide-based materials for SIBs (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b21803/suppl_file/am9b21803_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b21803/suppl_file/am9b21803_si_001.pdf">am9b21803_si_001.pdf (1.69 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});

})();

<script nonce="90f6ece82ec6775c-LHR">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

)|sy(01|mb)|t2(18|50)|t6(00|10|18)|ta(gt|lk)|tcl\-|tdg\-|tel(i|m)|tim\-|t\-mo|to(pl|sh)|ts(70|m\-|m3|m5)|tx\-9|up(\.b|g1|si)|utst|v400|v750|veri|vi(rg|te)|vk(40|5[0-3]|\-v)|vm40|voda|vulc|vx(52|53|60|61|70|80|81|83|85|98)|w3c(\-| )|webc|whit|wi(g |nc|nw)|wmlb|wonu|x700|yas\-|your|zeto|zte\-/i.test(a.substr(0,4))) check = true;})(navigator.userAgent||navigator.vendor||window.opera);
              return check;
        };

    var _isMobile = window.mobilecheck();
    if (_isMobile) {
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').addClass('mobile');
    }

    var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage = "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

    function init() {
        setTimeout(function() {
            var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
            if (cookieExist) {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
                return false;
            } else {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
                gdprMessage();
            }
            //Events
            $('#closebtn').on("click", hideForm);

            //Handle submit
            $('#gdpr-message-btn').on("click", function(event) {
                handleClick();
            });

            // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
            // $(document).click(function(event) {
            // 	event.stopPropagation();
            //   console.log(event.target);
            //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
            //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
            //     $(this).off();
            //   }
            // });
            $('#gdpr-con-btn').click(function() {
                setCookie("gdpr", "true");
                hideForm();
            });
        }, time);
    }

    //Show the message
    function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $('#gdpr-message-modal').show();
    }

    function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
            //Submit the form
            //Hide form
            if ($('.gdpr_err')) {
                $('.gdpr_err').hide();
            }

            $("#gdpr-message-content")
                //If successful then...
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
            //Show error message
            gdprErrorMessage();
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
    }

    function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
            return false;
        } else {
            errorStatus = true;
            $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
    }

    function validateEmail(email) {
        var re = /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
    }

    function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
    }

    function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + '=([^;]+)'));
        if (match) return match[1];
    }

    function hideForm() { //And set cookie
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag('event', 'GDPR Modal', { 'event_category': 'Pubs GDPR', 'event_label':'GDPR Dismissal'});
    }

    return {
        init: init
    }
})();

$(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
</script>

var currentJournal = "ACS Applied Materials &amp;amp; Interfaces";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
